---
layout: "post"
title: "HoTT exercises"
date: "2018-04-08"
categories: type-theory
toc: true
---

This is a self-contained version of some solutions for HoTT-Book's exercises.
The idea is to unpackage all as long as possible to get a better understanding.
Many changes can appear running this experiment. Solutions are
type-checked as a whole using Agda v2.5.3.

## Requirements

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agda has a pragma to work with HoTT:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="516" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="520" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="528" class="Option">--without-K</a> <a id="540" class="Symbol">#-}</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Equality type definition also called Identity type:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="703" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="709" class="Number">4</a> <a id="711" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">_≡_</a>

## Chapter 1

### Exercise 1.1

{: .exercise}
  Given functions $$f : A \to B$$ and $$g:B\to C$$, define
  their composite $$ g\circ f:A\to C$$.
  Show that we have $$h \circ (g\circ f) \equiv (h\circ g)\circ f$$.


We define the composition operation in Agda as follows.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="_∘_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">_∘_</a> <a id="2104" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2106" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="2108" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2109" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2109" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="2111" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2111" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="2113" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2113" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2114" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="2116" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2117" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2119" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2121" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2125" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2109" class="Bound">i</a><a id="2126" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2128" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2130" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2132" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2136" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2111" class="Bound">j</a><a id="2137" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2139" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="2141" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2143" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2147" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2113" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2148" class="Symbol">}</a>
    <a id="2154" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2156" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2157" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2159" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2161" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a><a id="2162" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2168" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2170" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2171" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2173" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2175" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2128" class="Bound">B</a><a id="2176" class="Symbol">)</a>
    <a id="2182" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2184" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2117" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2186" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2188" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2139" class="Bound">C</a>
<a id="2190" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2190" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2192" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">∘</a> <a id="2194" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2194" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2196" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="2198" class="Symbol">λ</a> <a id="2200" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2200" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="2202" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2204" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2190" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="2206" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2207" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2194" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="2209" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2200" class="Bound">x</a><a id="2210" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Then, the `∘-assoc` shows us that associativity of this composition holds.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="∘-assoc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%88%98-assoc" class="Function">∘-assoc</a> <a id="2321" class="Symbol">:</a> <a ### Exercise 1.2

<div class="exercise">
Derive the recursion principle for products $$\mathsf{rec}_{A\times B}$$
using only the projections, and verify that the definitional equalities
are valid. Do the same for $$\Sigma$$-types.
</div>

To solve this problem we need to know:

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}
      : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) → A \times B \to C.
    $$
    </p>

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}
      : \prod\limits_{(C : U)} (\Pi_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C) \rightarrow
        \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C
    $$
    </p>

<div class="proof" id="proof-1.2">
Proof.<br/>
For products:<br/>
If we have the projections,
$$\mathsf{proj}_1 : A \times B \to \mathsf{A}$$ and $$\mathsf{proj}_2 : A \times B \to \mathsf{B}$$,
then $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$ is another inhabitant where

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
&\mathsf{rec}_1 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) \to A \times B \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_1~C~g~c~:\equiv~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c,~\mathsf{proj}_2 c).
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_1$$.
<br/>
<br/>
For sums:<br/>
The projections are $$\mathsf{proj}_1 : \sum_{x : A}  Bx \to \mathsf{A}$$ and
$$\mathsf{proj}_2 :  \prod_{(p : \sum_{x : A}  Bx)} \to \mathsf{B} (\mathsf{proj}_1 p)$$.<br/>
By using these projections, we got another recursor defined as follows:
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{aling*}
&\mathsf{rec}_2 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}}  (\prod_{x : A} Bx \to C) \to \sum\limits_{x : A} B x \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_2~C~g~c~=~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c)~(\mathsf{proj}_2 c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>

By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$.
</div>

the following exercises including this one:

that we provide.

  <a id="5317" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="5322" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">Σ-Def₁</a> <a id="5329" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="5335" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="5336" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5338" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5340" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%81" class="Field">proj₁</a><a id="5345" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5347" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3.proj%E2%82%82" class="Field">proj₂</a><a id="5352" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="5354" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="5358" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="Σ-Rec₁.rec" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="5367" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="5369" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="5371" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5234" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="5373" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5245" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="5375" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="5377" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#5260" class="Bound">C</a>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the other hand, the product type is just a particular case of the sigma type
when the codomain is not dependent, as we can see next by omitting the argument
in `(λ _ → B)`.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="5763" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">×-Def₁</a> <a id="5777" class="Keyword">where</a>

Its recursor with a function $$g : A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C$$ that we provide.

### Exercise 1.3

<p class="exercise">
Derive the induction principle for products $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$,
using only the projections and the propositional uniqueness principle
$$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$.
Verify that the definitional equalities are valid.
</p>

To solve this problem, recall the uniqueness principle (Pp. 29. HoTT-Book)

- The **propositional uniqueness principle** says that
every element of $$A\times B$$ is equal to a pair.

<p class="equation">
  $$ \mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}
     : \prod_{(x : A \times B)} ((\mathsf{proj}_{1}(x) , \mathsf{proj}_{2}(x))
       \equiv_{A\times B} x).
  $$
</p>

Product type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6930" class="Comment">-- this would be trivial in agda due to definitional η for records</a>
<a id="6997" class="Comment">-- so Capriotti defined a product type without η:</a>
<a id="7047" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="×-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="7061" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="7819" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a> <a id="7828" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7833" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7835" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>

        <a id="7893" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7895" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7866" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7897" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7899" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7868" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7901" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7903" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7876" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="7905" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7907" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7878" class="Bound">z</a> <a id="7909" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="7911" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7912" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7866" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="7914" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7916" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7876" class="Bound">y</a><a id="7917" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="7919" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="7921" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="7922" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7868" class="Bound">w</a> <a id="7924" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="7926" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#7878" class="Bound">z</a><a id="7927" class="Symbol">)</a>
  <a id="7931" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.pair%3D" class="Function">pair=</a> <a id="7937" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7942" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7947" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7949" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The induction principle for the product type:

<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B} : \prod\limits_{C : A \times B \to \mathcal{U}}
  \left( \prod\limits_{x:A}\ \prod\limits_{y:B}\ \,C( (x,y) ) \right)
  \to \prod\limits_{x:A \times B}\ \,C(x)
$$
</p>

          <a id="8564" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8566" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8567" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8567" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8569" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8571" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8572" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8572" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8574" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8576" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8263" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8577" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8579" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8579" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8581" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8583" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8274" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8584" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8586" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8588" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8535" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8590" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8591" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8572" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8593" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8595" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8579" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8596" class="Symbol">))</a>
          <a id="8609" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8611" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8612" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8612" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8614" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8616" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8263" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8617" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8619" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8621" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8623" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8274" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8624" class="Symbol">)</a>
          <a id="8636" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8638" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind" class="Function">ind</a> <a id="8642" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8535" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8644" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8567" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8646" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8647" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8612" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8649" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8651" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8652" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8654" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="8656" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8567" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8658" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8612" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8660" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8619" class="Bound">y</a>
  <a id="8664" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind-%CE%B2" class="Function">ind-β</a> <a id="8670" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8670" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8672" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8672" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8674" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8674" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8676" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8676" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8678" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8680" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

<p class="exercise">
Generalize $$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$ to Σ-types, and do the same for
$$\Sigma$$-types, i.e. show induction and verify the definitional equality
is valid.
</p>

Σ-type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="8928" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Def₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Def₂</a> <a id="8942" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="Σ-Def₂.Σ._,_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a> <a id="9018" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9020" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="9021" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9021" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9023" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9025" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8964" class="Bound">A</a><a id="9026" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="9028" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9030" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8975" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9032" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9021" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="9034" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9036" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82.%CE%A3" class="Datatype">Σ</a> <a id="9038" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8964" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9040" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8975" class="Bound">B</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Its induction principle:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="9423" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Σ-Ind₂" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Ind%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Ind₂</a> <a id="9437" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="9438" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9438" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="9440" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9440" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9441" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9443" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9443" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9445" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9447" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9451" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9438" class="Bound">i</a><a id="9452" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="9454" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9454" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="9456" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="9458" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9443" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="9460" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="9462" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="9466" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#9440" class="Bound">j</a><a id="9467" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="9469" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="9477" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="9482" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">Σ-Def₂</a> <a id="9489" class="Keyword">public</a>

### Exercise 1.4

<div class="exercise">
Assuming as given only the <em>iterator</em> for natural numbers
<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ite} : \prod\limits_{C:\mathcal{U}} C \to (C \to C) \to \mathbb{N} \to C $$
</p>
with the defining equations
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,0)               &\equiv c_0, \\
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,\mathsf{suc}(n)) &\equiv c_s(\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
derive a function having the type of the recursor $$\mathsf{rec}$$.
Show that the defining equations of the recursor hold propositionally for this
function, using the induction principle for $$\mathbb{N}$$.
</div>

To solve this problem, let us define the recursor and also the induction principle
for natural numbers. (See more details about these functions in
[Induction on Natural Numbers]({% post_url 2018-02-12-induction-on-natural-numbers %})).

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="10741" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="ℕ-Def" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a> <a id="10754" class="Keyword">where</a>

    <a id="ℕ-Def.ℕ.suc" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a>  <a id="10804" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="10806" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a> <a id="10808" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="10810" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a>

  <a id="10985" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="10990" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a>

       <a id="11027" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11029" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11030" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11007" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11032" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a><a id="11036" class="Symbol">)</a>
       <a id="11045" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11047" class="Symbol">(∀</a> <a id="11050" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11051" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11051" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11053" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="11055" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="11056" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="11058" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11060" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11007" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11062" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11051" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11064" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="11066" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11007" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11068" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11069" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.suc" class="InductiveConstructor">suc</a> <a id="11073" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11051" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11074" class="Symbol">))</a>

Now, we define the iterator following the equations above:

Then, we now can define the recursor using this `ite` by iterating over the type
`ℕ × C` (*reloading recursion*?).


<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="11594" class="Comment">-- recursor</a>
  <a id="11608" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="11613" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82" class="Module">×-Def₂</a> <a id="11620" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="11626" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11627" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">_×_</a><a id="11630" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11632" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%81" class="Function">proj₁</a><a id="11637" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11639" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82.proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">proj₂</a><a id="11644" class="Symbol">;</a> <a id="11646" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_,_</a><a id="11649" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="11707" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Fun.rec%E2%82%82" class="Function">rec₂</a> <a id="11712" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11712" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="11714" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11714" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="11717" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11717" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="11720" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11720" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="11722" class="Symbol">=</a>

           <a id="11754" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11755" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95.zero" class="InductiveConstructor">zero</a> <a id="11760" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="11762" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11714" class="Bound">c₀</a><a id="11764" class="Symbol">)</a>
           <a id="11777" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="11780" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="11781" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11781" class="Bound">p</a> <a            <a id="11847" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11720" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11848" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, we need to establish the propositional equality between these two
definitions of recursor, i.e, between `rec` and `rec₂`. Let's use
induction to prove that.

      <a id="12738" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12674" class="Function">u</a> <a id="12740" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12742" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.ap-proj%E2%82%82" class="Function">ap-proj₂</a>  <a id="12752" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="12753" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="12755" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12757" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="12758" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="12760" class="Argument">B</a> <a id="12762" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="12764" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12377" class="Bound">C</a><a id="12765" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="12767" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="12768" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#ex1-4.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="12774" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12377" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="12776" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12379" class="Bound">c₀</a> <a id="12779" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12382" class="Bound">cₛ</a> <a id="12782" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#12390" class="Bound">n</a><a id="12783" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


### Exercise 1.5

<div class="exercise">

Show that if we define

  $$A+B :\equiv \sum\limits_{(x : \mathbbbold{2})} \mathsf{rec}_{\mathbbbold{2}} (\mathcal{U}, A , B, x),$$

then we can give a definition of $$\ind\limits_{A + B}$$ for which the
definitional equalities holds.

</div>

To solve this problem, let us introduce the $$\mathcal{2}$$ type, that is, the
type with two constructors also called **Bool**. The constructors are also called
false and true respectively.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="13288" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="13302" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="13311" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="13318" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13320" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="13324" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="13336" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13338" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟙" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="13346" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13348" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, let's try to define the recursor for this coproduct, and later,
we'll try the dependent version of it to complete the exercise.

      <a id="14547" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14549" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14484" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="14551" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="14553" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14486" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="14555" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14557" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14498" class="Bound">C</a>

  <a id="14585" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="14589" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14589" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14591" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14591" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14593" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14594" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="14596" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="14598" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14598" class="Bound">b</a><a id="14599" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14601" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14603" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14591" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14605" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14598" class="Bound">b</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Notice how the recursor of the coproduct matches with the elimination
rule of the disjunction conective also called *case analysis*. That's follows from the
[**propositions-as-types**](https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/propositions+as+types).

![path](/assets/latexit-images/disj-elimination.png)

Finally, the induction principle for the coproduct:

### Exercise 1.6

<div class="exercise" id="ex-1.6">
Show that if we define $$A \times B :≡ \prod_{x:\mathbf{2}}\mathsf{rec}_{\mathbf{2}}\ (\mathcal{U}\, A\, B\, x)$$,
then we can give a definition of $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$ for which the definitional
equalities propositionally (i.e. using equality types).
</div>

### Exercise 1.8

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.8">

Define multiplication and exponentiation using $$\mathsf{rec}{\mathbb{N}}$$.
Verify that $$(\mathbb{N},+,0,\times,1)$$ is a semiring using only
$$\ind{\mathbb{N}}$$.

</div>

### Exercise 1.9

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.9">

Define the type family $$\mathsf{Fin} : \mathbb{N} \to \mathcal{U}$$ mentioned
at the end of Section 1.3, and the dependent function $$\mathsf{fmax} :
\prod_{n:\mathbb{N}} \mathsf{Fin}(n+1)$$ mentioned in Section 1.4.
</div>

### Exercise 1.11

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.11">
Show that for any type $$A$$, we have $$\neg\neg\neg A \to \neg A$$.
</div>

A propositional logic proof using [Agda-Prop](http://github.com/jonaprieto/agda-prop)
library:

                  <a id="19591" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="19592" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#weaken" class="InductiveConstructor">weaken</a> <a id="19599" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="19600" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="19602" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#19365" class="Bound">A</a><a id="19603" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="19605" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="19606" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#assume" class="InductiveConstructor">assume</a> <a id="19613" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="19614" class="Argument">Γ</a> <a id="19616" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="19618" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#19362" class="Bound">Γ</a> <a id="19620" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%2C_" class="Function Operator">,</a> <a id="19622" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="19624" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="19626" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="19628" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#19365" class="Bound">A</a><a id="19629" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="19631" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#19365" class="Bound">A</a><a id="19632" class="Symbol">))))))</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

In type theory, the term is:

$$
λ (x : ((A → ⊥) → ⊥) → ⊥) (a : A) . x ((λ h : A → ⊥) . ha) :
((A → ⊥) → ⊥) → ⊥) → (A → ⊥)
$$

### Exercise 1.16

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.16">
Show that addition of natural numbers is commutative:
<p class="equation">
$$
\prod\limits_{i,j : \mathbb{N}}\ (i + j = j + i).
$$
</p>
</div>

## Chapter 2

### Exercise 2.6

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.6">
Prove that if $$p : x \equiv y$$, then the function
$$(p \cdot -) : (y \equiv z) \to (x \equiv z)$$ is an equivalence.
</div>

### Exercise 2.10

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.10">
Prove that ∑-types are associative, in that for any $$A : \mathcal{U}$$
and families $$B : A  \to U$$ and $$C : \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \to \mathcal{U}$$,
we have
<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \simeq \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
</div>

<div class="proof" id="proof-2.10">
Solution.<br/>
We can prove that the following functions $$f$$ and $$g$$ are inverses.

<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \overset{f}{\underset{g}{\rightleftarrows}} \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
defined by $$f(a,b,c) :\equiv ((a,b),c)$$, $$g(z,c) :\equiv (\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)$$.<br/>
Indeed,
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(f \circ g) (z, c) &:\equiv f (g (z,c))\\
&:\equiv f\,(\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)\\
&:\equiv ((\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z), c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
</div>

        <a id="21764" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="21766" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21767" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21767" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="21769" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="21771" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="21773" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21715" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="21775" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="21778" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21778" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="21780" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="21782" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3" class="Record">Σ</a> <a id="21784" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21785" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21725" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="21787" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21778" class="Bound">a</a><a id="21788" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="21790" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="21793" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21793" class="Bound">b</a> <a id="21795" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="21797" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21739" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="21799" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21800" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21778" class="Bound">a</a> <a id="21802" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="21804" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21793" class="Bound">b</a><a id="21805" class="Symbol">))))</a>

### Exercise 2.13

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.13">
Show that $$(2 \simeq 2) \simeq 2$$.
</div>


### Exercise 2.14

<div class="exercise">

  Suppose we add to type theory [the equality reflection
  rule](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IlfQjWqrK6I) which says that if there is
  an element $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,y) $$, then in fact $$ x :\equiv y$$. Prove
  that for any $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,x)$$ we have $$p :\equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.\\

  <p class="equation">
  $$
    \begin{prooftree}
    \AxiomC{$\vdash p : \mathsf{Id}(x, y)$}
    \RightLabel{$\mathsf{Eq}$}
    \UnaryInfC{$\vdash x \equiv y.$}
    \end{prooftree}
    $$

  </p>

</div>

<div class="proof">
  Proof.<br/>
  We first fix the type of $$\mathsf{refl}_x$$ in order to apply effectively
  path induction.<br/>

  <p class="equation">
    $$
    \begin{prooftree}
    \AxiomC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ p : x = y$}
    \RightLabel{$\mathsf{Eq}$}
    \UnaryInfC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ x ≡ y$}
    \AxiomC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ \mathsf{refl}_x : x = x$}
    \BinaryInfC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ \mathsf{refl}_x : x = y.$}
    \end{prooftree}
    $$
    </p>
  Now, $$\mathsf{refl}_x$$ and $$p : x = y$$ in the formulation of path induction
  is well-typed. Therefore, by path induction, we show that
  $$\mathsf{Id}(p,\mathsf{refl_{x}})$$. Let be $$x : A$$ and $$C :\equiv
  \prod_{y : A} \prod_{p : x \equiv y }\ p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_{x}$$.
  It sufficies to show and inhabitant of $$C(x, \mathsf{refl}_{x})$$, and it is,
  $$\mathsf{refl}_{\mathsf{refl}_x} : \mathsf{refl}_x = \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
  By equation reflection rule, since we have an inhabitant of $$p \equiv
  \mathsf{refl}_x$$, these are judgemental equal,i.e., $$p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.

### Exercise 2.17

<div class="exercise">
<ul>
  <li> Show that if $$A \simeq A$$  and $$B \simeq B'$$, then $$(A\times B) \simeq (A'\times B')$$. </li>
  <li> Give two proofs of this fact, one using univalence and one not using it, and show that the two proofs are equal.</li>
  <li> Formulate and prove analogous results for the other type formers: $$\Sigma$$, $$\to$$, $$\Pi$$, and $$+$$. </li>
</ul>
</div>


## Chapter 3

To solve the following exercises, let us recall a few things:

- The *set* definition in HoTT:

A type $$A$$ is a **set** if for all $$x, y : A$$ and
all $$p, q : x \equiv y$$, we have $$ p \equiv q$$. In a proposition
we have

$$
\mathsf{isSet}(A) :\equiv \prod\limits_{(x,y : A)}\prod\limits_{(p,q : x \equiv y)} (p \equiv q).
$$

- The type for equivalence from $$A$$ to $$B$$

$$
  (A \simeq B) :\equiv \sum\limits_{f : A \to B} \mathsf{isequiv}(f),
$$

where

$$
\mathsf{isequiv(f)} :\equiv
  \left (\sum\limits_{g : B \to A} (f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{B})\right) \times
  \left (\sum\limits_{h : B \to A} (h \circ f \sim \mathsf{id}_{A})\right)
$$

- The homotopy concept:

Let $$f , g : \prod\limits_{(x:A)} P(x)$$ be two sections of a
type family $$P : A \to \mathcal{U}$$. A **homotopy** from $$f$$ to $$g$$
is a dependent function of type

$$
(f \sim g) :\equiv \prod\limits_{x : A} (f(x) \equiv g(x)).
$$

### Exercise 3.1

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A\simeq B$$ and $$A$$ is a set, then so is $$B$$.
</div>


<div class="proof" id="proof-3.1">
Proof 1.<br/>
Let be $$x,y : B$$ and $$p : x \equiv_{B} y$$ and $$q : x \equiv_{B} y$$.
We need to prove $$ p \equiv q$$.<br/>
Since $$A\simeq B$$ then there is a function $$f : A \to B$$ and some
$$g : B \to A$$ such that $$f \circ g \sim id_{B}$$.
Using this function $$g$$ over the path $$p$$ we get
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} p : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
We do the same but this time over the path $$q$$, that is,
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} q : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
Because of $$A$$ is a set, we have a new path called
$$m :\mathsf{ap}_{g} p \equiv_{gx \equiv_{A} gy} \mathsf{ap}_{g} q$$. <br/>

Now, an action over this path $$m$$
using the function $$\mathsf{ap}_{f} : x \equiv_{A} y \to f x \equiv_{B} f y$$
will give us


$$
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m :
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q).
$$


By the lemmas in Chapter 2, we do the following reasoning:

$$
\begin{align*}
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q) &=
  \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} q\\
  &=(\text{transporting by using} f \sim g)\\
  &=\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} q\\
  &=p \equiv q.
\end{align*}
$$

Then, we have the inhabitant, $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m : p \equiv q$$.
</div>

### Exercise 3.2

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A$$ and $$B$$ are sets, then so is $$A+B$$.
</div>

To solve this exercise, we should take a look of some results from Chapter 2,
Section 2.12.

<div class="proof" id="proof-3.2">
Proof.<br/>

Let be $$x, y : A + B$$, and paths $$p : x \equiv y$$, $$q : x \equiv
y$$. Let's get a path $$p \equiv q$$.  We proceed by case analysis. If
$$x :\equiv \mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, for
some $$a, b : A$$ then $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p : a
\equiv_{A} b$$ and $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q : a \equiv_{A}
b$$.

Since $$A$$ is a set, there is a path between these last two terms,
this is, $$m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p \equiv
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q$$.  Now, an action over this path
$$m$$ using the $$\mathsf{inl}$$ function give us:
$$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}} m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q)$$.<br/>

By path algebra we get $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
m : p \equiv q$$ since $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv p$$.<br/> Following the
same reasoning, we prove the case $$x :\equiv \mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y
:\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$.  For the latest cases, $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$ and $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, we use the
encode-decode method to derive a proof term for 𝟘 from
$$p$$ and $$q$$. Then, we may conclude anything we wish, that is, $$p
\equiv q$$.
</div>

In Agda.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="28373" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟘-Def" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%98-Def" class="Module">𝟘-Def</a> <a id="28386" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="28394" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟘-Def.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%98-Def.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="Datatype">𝟘</a> <a id="28401" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="28403" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="28407" class="Keyword">where</a>

<a id="28414" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟘-Rec" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%98-Rec" class="Module">𝟘-Rec</a> <a id="28427" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="29045" class="Comment">-- ind : {A B : Set}</a>
  <a id="29068" class="Comment">--     → (C : A + B → Set)</a>
  <a id="29097" class="Comment">--     → ((x : A) → C (inl x))</a>
  <a id="29130" class="Comment">--     → ((x : B) → C (inr x))</a>
  <a id="29163" class="Comment">--     → (x : A + B) → C x</a>

### Exercise 3.3

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$ A $$ is a set and $$B : A \to \mathcal{U}$$
is a type family such that $$B(x)$$ is a set for all
$$x : A$$, then $$\Sigma\limits_{(x:A)}\ B(x)$$ is a set.
</div>

### Exercise 3.4

<div class="exercise">
Show that $$A$$ is a mere proposition if and only
if $$A\to A$$ is contractible.
</div>
